<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0f28d13f-af6b-4968-bb1d-81fda6324a0c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer5804748189304752668"><b>”...And then shall arise a contemptible one whom royal majesty has not been given. He shall come by counterfeit means and obtain the Kingdom of flatteries. Armies shall be swept away before him and broken...and he shall act deceitfully and he shall become strong with a small people. Without warning he shall come into the richest parts; and he shall do what neither his fathers nor his fathers’ fathers have done, scattering among the people plunder, spoils, and goods. He shall devise plans against</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5804748189304752668" style="display:none"><b>”...And then shall arise a contemptible one whom royal majesty has not been given. He shall come by counterfeit means and obtain the Kingdom of flatteries. Armies shall be swept away before him and broken...and he shall act deceitfully and he shall become strong with a small people. Without warning he shall come into the richest parts; and he shall do what neither his fathers nor his fathers’ fathers have done, scattering among the people plunder, spoils, and goods. He shall devise plans against strongholds, he shall exalt himself and magnify himself above every God, and shall speak astonishing things against the God of Gods. He shall prosper until the indignation is accomplished, for what is determined shall be done.”</b><br><br><a href="http://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/TheOmen_zps44e278bd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382975959i/6312236._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo TheOmen_zps44e278bd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>The movie poster for the 1976 version starring Gregory Peck and Lee Remick.</b><br><br>Jeremy Thorn and his wife Katherine have been struggling to conceive. Katherine teeters on the edge of the precipice of insanity. They believe that if only they could have a child it would give Katherine something more to focus on than her own unhappiness. They have miscarried a couple of times and now finally a pregnancy is coming to term. Katherine is hospitalized in the 8th month and the fears of losing yet another child are gnawing at their already shattered nerves.<br><br>She loses the child…but wait.<br><br>Father Spilletto pulls Jeremy Thorn aside and said “do I have a deal for you” (and the devil deals the cards). A child is presented to Thorn. A cherub, healthy, and the wife doesn’t ever have to know. Thorn overwhelmed with emotions and realizing what losing another child will do to his wife...accepts. I could almost hear the whisk whisk of the priest rubbing his hands together with satisfaction over another bargain made. <br><br>The child is in place. His name is Damien.<br><br>Haven’t we all at times wondering if our child was the spawn of satan? Those moments when their head starts spinning around on their shoulders and for a moment I am amused and even enthralled... well until the fish start falling from the sky and a cloud of locust descends. Grilled grasshopper as a side dish to fried fish is fine for a while, and better yet if the damn wine hasn’t been turned into blood, but it doesn’t take long for me to want them to officially declare themselves Demon or just an annoying little twerp. If they are a DEMON I can turn them over to a priest or make a call to Sam and Dean Winchester, but if they are just an annoying little twerp?<br><br>*Sigh*...then I have to keep trying to find ways to communicate and coexist with this entity.<br><br><a href="http://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/SamandDeanWinchester_zps3fb2f1d1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382975959i/6312237.jpg" alt=" photo SamandDeanWinchester_zps3fb2f1d1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Sam and Dean are on my speed dial.</b><br><br>Damien is an odd little fellow. <br><br><i>”He’s like a little man from Mars,” Horton once remarked to his wife. “Like he was sent here to study the human race.”</i><br><br>His first nanny hangs herself as an act of devotion to Damien. A Mrs. Blaylock appears and declares herself the new nanny. Jeremy and Katherine are suspicious, but not suspicious enough. Damien seems to like her and her devotion to his welfare is without question, but when she starts to push Katherine aside the Thorns find themselves locked in a battle with the “hired help” for time with their son. <br><br>A priest named Tassone arrives at Thorn’s office spouting gibberish and really he is too desperate for the salvation of his own soul to appear as anything other than a lunatic. He was for lack of a better term “the cleaner” for Spilletto. He has much to atone for. He has very little time to convince Thorn that his son is not what he seems or actually that he is exactly what he seems. The forces around Damien are starting to circle Tassone. <br><br>Jeremy soon finds himself on his way to Rome hoping for answers to explain what and who Damien is. What bargain did he really make with Father Spilletto? Who are those people in the grave North of Rome protected by dogs that could have stepped out of the script of a <i>Resident Evil</i> movie? <br><br><i>”The bushes began to rustle and another dog’s head appeared; this one gray, its muzzle disfigured and dripping. Then another appeared, and another, the cemetery coming alive with motion as the darkened figures emerged from everywhere, a pack of at least ten, insane and ravenous, their mouths dripping in a continual drool.”</i><br><br>A Devil Child’s best friends. <br><br>The dying words of a priest send Thorn to Jerusalem to track down a man named Bugenhagen, the last of a long line of exorcists. He is living underground at the heart of the beginning of Christianity in the City of Jezreel, town of Meggido. It is the only place where he is safe. He explains to Thorn what he must do. <br><br><a href="http://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/TheOmen2006_zps471f6d07.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382975959i/6312238.jpg" alt=" photo TheOmen2006_zps471f6d07.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>The 2006 remake of The Omen stars the lovely Julia Stiles, Seamus Davey-Fitzpatrick and Liev Schrieber</b><br><br>This book launched a franchise of books and movies. Even though I had a good idea of the plot it didn’t detract from my enjoyment of the book. I will certainly be on the look out for signs of the Diabolical Trinity. <b>”The Devil, The Anti-Christ, and The False Prophet.</b> If your children or your grandchildren are born with a full head of hair find a reason to shave their head and look for a trinity of numbers that will send a shiver down to your toes...666. I hope you don’t find them. This is another entry in my 1970s nostalgic horror tour. <br><br>If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br>I also have a Facebook blogger page at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5804748189304752668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2509638628247432276">The Omen, David Seltzer<br/><br/>Jeremy Thorn, United States Ambassador to England, and his wife Katherine become the parents of a beautiful boy whose destiny is to fulfill the most horrible prophecy ever made.<br/><br/>The Omen is a 1976 English-language supernatural horror film directed by Richard Donner, and written by David Seltzer. The film stars Gregory Peck, Lee Remick, David Warner, Harvey Spencer Stephens, Billie Whitelaw, Patrick Troughton, Martin Benson, and Leo McKern. <br/><br/>The first installment of The Omen </span>
  <span id="freeText2509638628247432276" style="display:none">The Omen, David Seltzer<br /><br />Jeremy Thorn, United States Ambassador to England, and his wife Katherine become the parents of a beautiful boy whose destiny is to fulfill the most horrible prophecy ever made.<br /><br />The Omen is a 1976 English-language supernatural horror film directed by Richard Donner, and written by David Seltzer. The film stars Gregory Peck, Lee Remick, David Warner, Harvey Spencer Stephens, Billie Whitelaw, Patrick Troughton, Martin Benson, and Leo McKern. <br /><br />The first installment of The Omen franchise, The Omen concerns a young child replaced at birth by American Ambassador Robert Thorn unbeknownst to his wife, after their own son was murdered at the hospital, enabling the son of Satan to grow up with wealth and power. They are surrounded by mysterious and ominous deaths, unaware that the child, Damien, is the Antichrist.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز سی و یکم ماه می سال 1998 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: طالع نحس؛ اثر دیوید سلتزر؛ برگردان شهریار نیرومند؛ مشخصات نشر تهران، نشر سمیر، 1376، در 335ص، شابک: 9649038116، داستانهای آمریکایی سده 20م<br /><br />این فیلم برای نخستین بار در ایران در «جشنواره جهانی فیلم تهران» به نمایش درآمد؛ چند هفته پس از پایان جشنواره، نمایش عمومی آن در سینماهای پارامونت و شهرقصه در تهران آغاز شد؛ تماشای این فیلم برای اشخاص کمتر از هجده سال قدغن اعلام شده بود؛ بعلت اعتصاب دوبلورهای حرفه‌ ای و باسابقه در آن زمان، برای دوبله ی این فیلم از دوبلورهای تازه‌ کار و کم تجربه استفاده شده بود، که حالت سرد و بیروحی به فیلم داده بود، ولی برحسب تصادف این سردی دوبله، بطرز عجیبی، با فضای رعب‌آور و خوفناک فیلم، هماهنگی داشت، و وحشت و اضطراب آن را بمراتب بیشتر کرده بود؛ پیش از نمایش فیلم در ایران، کتاب آن به فارسی ترجمه و بصورت پاورقی در مجله هفتگی بانوان چاپ می‌شد<br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_2851867083" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2851867083" />
    <a title="RedemptionDenied" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55677020-redemptiondenied"><img alt="RedemptionDenied" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2851867083?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RedemptionDenied" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RedemptionDenied" href="/user/show/55677020-redemptiondenied">RedemptionDenied</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=conspiracy">conspiracy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=demon-scum">demon-scum</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=gory">gory</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=apocalyptic">apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=betrayal">betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2851867083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1215046480291412366">3.5 - 4.0<br/><br/>"Let He who hath understanding <br/>Reckon the number of the Beast; <br/>For it is a human number,<br/>It's number is Six Hundred and Sixty Six."<br/> Revelations<br/><br/>This is another case, where I've seen the movie (1976) before reading the book. I loved the movie (not the 2006 remake); and enjoyed the novel - just as much, mostly - though I think the movie was, slightly, better. Some of the death-scenes played-out differently, and Thorn's visit to Meggido, where Yigael's Wall is situated in the Old City of Jez</span>
  <span id="freeText1215046480291412366" style="display:none">3.5 - 4.0<br /><br />"Let He who hath understanding <br />Reckon the number of the Beast; <br />For it is a human number,<br />It's number is Six Hundred and Sixty Six."<br /> Revelations<br /><br />This is another case, where I've seen the movie (1976) before reading the book. I loved the movie (not the 2006 remake); and enjoyed the novel - just as much, mostly - though I think the movie was, slightly, better. Some of the death-scenes played-out differently, and Thorn's visit to Meggido, where Yigael's Wall is situated in the Old City of Jezreel - and has the image of the Anti-Christ (Damien) wasn't in the book (or is it in Damien: Omen 2? I can't remember now. Haven't seen the movies, for eons). He went to Israel with Jennings to find Bugenhagen - but didn't see the Wall. Why? It wasn't even mentioned. Why? As a marketing stratagem, the book preceded the movie by two-weeks. <br /><br />I loved the soundtrack, as well, which was used to great dramatic-effect; especially when something bad was about to happen. Jerry Goldsmith won an Oscar for Best Original Score. I think the graveyard scene creeped-me-out the most, when Thorne opens the graves and sees what lies within. It's like revelations. After the movie was shown: there was an influx of people wanting to own Rottweilers, for some reason. The scene in the elevator (Omen 2), ensured I took the stairs, regardless how many flights I had to ascend. <br /><br />The 1976 film, had a budget of $2.8 million and took $60.9 million at the Box office, compared to the 2006 (pointless) remake, which took $119.5 million at the Box office. <br /><br />1976 cast:<br /><br />Gregory Peck (Robert Thorn)<br />Harvey Spencer Stephens (Damien Thorn)<br />Lee Remick (Katherine Thorn)<br />David Warner (Keith Jennings)<br />Billie Whitelaw (Mrs. Baylock)<br />Patrick Troughton (Father Brennan)<br />Holly Palance (Nanny) - didn't know Jack Palance's daughter was in the film.<br />Martin Benson (Father Spilletto)<br /><br />"It happened in a millisecond. A movement in the galaxies that should have taken eons, occurred in the blinking of an eye."<br /><br />And so it begins...<br /><br />American Diplomat, Robert Thorn, is visiting a hospital in Rome, where his wife, Kathy, is about to give birth. When he reaches the hospital, he's told, his child is dead, 'It breathed for a moment,' whispered the priest, 'then breathed no more.' He's advised that his wife is safe, but will be unable to bear another child. She's been pregnant twice-before which were still-born, this one went to full-term and died - unbeknownst to Thorn - with a little intervention. <br /><br />In another part of the hospital, a mother has given birth: where the child survived and the mother died. The priest tells him, he could adopt. 'It's a foundling,' said the priest. ' It's mother died as your own child...in the same hour.' And so begins Thorn's deception. He can't - won't - tell his wife, she's lost another child. It'd destroy her.<br /><br />Only three people are privy to the child's true nature: Father Spilletto, Sister Teresa and Father Tasscone. And only one of those, eventually, has a conscience. I liked the background-history on Tasscone; and how he became part of the covenant in Rome - that was quite amusing. He wants absolution for his transgressions. Er.. redemption denied.<br /><br />Playlist:<br /><br />● "The Number Of The Beast," Iron Maiden.<br />● "O Fortuna," Carl Orff/Wagner.<br />● "Shout At The Devil," Motley Crue.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1215046480291412366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2208951775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2208951775" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10477405-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340652114p2/10477405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2208951775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12876064896713526650">Absolute classic! It add some details to the fantastic movie and is a pageturning read. Gosh, what a story. A must read for every fan of horror literature. One of the most gripping tales ever and extremely eerie. This is one of the books you'll never forget!</span>

          </span>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2208951775">
  <td colspan="2">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2392621965?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2392621965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14667514838346151785"><i>“Here is wisdom. Let him that hath understanding count the number of the beast; for it is the number of a man; and his number is 666”</i><br/><br/>Cue that ominous Gregorian choir music from the original 1976 film. That was one of my all-time favorite movies, and I’ve seen it so many times, I was actually anticipating the dialogue as I read the novel. But that didn’t diminish the read one bit. For those who don’t know the story (spoilers) … it’s about the birth of the devil’s child, and the ruin of the family</span>
  <span id="freeText14667514838346151785" style="display:none"><i>“Here is wisdom. Let him that hath understanding count the number of the beast; for it is the number of a man; and his number is 666”</i><br /><br />Cue that ominous Gregorian choir music from the original 1976 film. That was one of my all-time favorite movies, and I’ve seen it so many times, I was actually anticipating the dialogue as I read the novel. But that didn’t diminish the read one bit. For those who don’t know the story (spoilers) … it’s about the birth of the devil’s child, and the ruin of the family who inadvertently raises him. It’s not so much scary, as it is dark, brooding, and chilling. The novel was written by the screenwriter of the film, and it was fascinating to see how he explored the sinister backgrounds behind some of the story’s more shadowy characters. It’s not at the level of “The Exorcist,” which for me is the pinnacle in this genre, but it’s still a gripping read. 4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14667514838346151785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2039141304" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/800291-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295167791p2/800291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2039141304?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/800291-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780860073710" href="/book/show/1309659.The_Omen">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2039141304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3254561633205096070">I have been meaning to read this book for years and never felt I had time to get round to it. Well this year being the year of finishing promises and completing challenges I thought it was about time. After all it repeatedly appears on lists of all time greatest horror books. <br/><br/>And so I started my reading of my 1981 edition (although it was first printed in the mid 70s) I started with a sense of deja-vu. Now I am sure I have never watched the film all the way through. First being too young (and ye</span>
  <span id="freeText3254561633205096070" style="display:none">I have been meaning to read this book for years and never felt I had time to get round to it. Well this year being the year of finishing promises and completing challenges I thought it was about time. After all it repeatedly appears on lists of all time greatest horror books. <br /><br />And so I started my reading of my 1981 edition (although it was first printed in the mid 70s) I started with a sense of deja-vu. Now I am sure I have never watched the film all the way through. First being too young (and yes scared) to watch it and then older and more skeptical of an ageing film. <br /><br />And yet so many scenes are familiar to me - maybe I have seen the film, or maybe these scenes have been repeated and reused in homage and recognition of their ground breaking nature. As I have to say for its age it does strike a punch. <br /><br />Now yes there are signs of its age - from smoking on aeroplanes to mention the use of film in cameras. However many of the more visual scenes are expertly written playing out literally like a film score. Playing on apprehension and atmosphere you can feel the tension rise - not bad for something like I say that is so famous many would feel it has no more surprises left to give. <br /><br />Looking back I think a lot of the book plays on paranoia of the coming ages - the fear of what is around the corner with the millennium approaching, political and economical unrest (I was born in the 70s and remember some of those tensions) I think some of the power of this story has now been bleached away. <br /><br />However there is still some underlying fear I think that will never go away and for this I can see why this book still sits on the best horror book lists. Just be ready for that feeling of deja-vu</span>
  <a data-text-id="3254561633205096070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1791352323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1791352323" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1791352323?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780860073710" href="/book/show/1309659.The_Omen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=films">films</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=mystery-horror">mystery-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1791352323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7187394193670689612">If I hadn't read this was a novelization of the incredibly chilling film starring Gregory Peck, by none other than David Seltzer himself, I would have rated it a bit higher. In a rare case, Seltzer has taken liberties with his own original material to transfer the film to the pages, and as it is, the novel seems like a very good effort. <br/><br/>It provides many interesting details about the past of key characters, especially Catherine, Thorn's wife, and father Tassone (who was father Brennan in the film</span>
  <span id="freeText7187394193670689612" style="display:none">If I hadn't read this was a novelization of the incredibly chilling film starring Gregory Peck, by none other than David Seltzer himself, I would have rated it a bit higher. In a rare case, Seltzer has taken liberties with his own original material to transfer the film to the pages, and as it is, the novel seems like a very good effort. <br /><br />It provides many interesting details about the past of key characters, especially Catherine, Thorn's wife, and father Tassone (who was father Brennan in the film). Also, the character of Jennings -my own personal favourite in both the film and the novel- the young photographer who helps Thorn solve the riddle concerning the boy Damien, is significantly expanded. <br /><br />The unfortunate thing is that there are some differences in comparison to the film that, in my opinion, are unecessary and take away much of the atmosphere that the film succeeds in creating. I will add no spoilers but I can say that while I definitely enjoyed reading the book, it failed to chill my blood and send shivers down my spine in the way the film did. I have watched the movie twice and will watch it again and again. Do I recommend the novelization? Certainly. Will I read it a second time? I doubt it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7187394193670689612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/40499770-the-omen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1108056-josh?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1108056-josh?shelf=read_2019">read_2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1108056-josh?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2647278160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer324194946982417244">Perhaps the best film tie in novel I've read. A perfect blend of subtle and overt horror tactics to scare the reader senseless. Author David Seltzer makes the son of Satan and the alignment of the end of days scarily plausible whilst somehow producing a character-centric read that's as enthralling as it is entertaining. <br/><br/>There's not much more I can say that hasn't already been said about this classic horror novel. <br/><br/>My rating: 5/5 stars. I've heard the sequels don't do the original justice but I'm </span>
  <span id="freeText324194946982417244" style="display:none">Perhaps the best film tie in novel I've read. A perfect blend of subtle and overt horror tactics to scare the reader senseless. Author David Seltzer makes the son of Satan and the alignment of the end of days scarily plausible whilst somehow producing a character-centric read that's as enthralling as it is entertaining. <br /><br />There's not much more I can say that hasn't already been said about this classic horror novel. <br /><br />My rating: 5/5 stars. I've heard the sequels don't do the original justice but I'm still keen to read Omen II, as for The Omen, I highly recommend it for horror fans.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)" href="/user/show/7487619-rachel-theshadesoforange">Rachel (TheShadesofOrange)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7487619-rachel-theshadesoforange?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7487619-rachel-theshadesoforange?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3214180698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9498402131634584762"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br/>This is one of those times where a story works better on screen than on the page. For a book about a demon child, I expected the boy to be a lot creepier. Instead this book was all about misdirection, which was annoying since we as the readers clearly knew that he was the source of the evil. While I didn't love the book, I am actually very interested in watching the movies because I think a visual narrative would work so much better. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2135178189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11201804409639248672">The movie adaptation of this short novel is synonymous with classic horror (and, somehow, I’ve yet to see it); the novel itself is worth a look, too. A quick, breezy ride into the occult and the destruction of a wealthy, famous family, there is a reason this story has been well-regarded for four decades and counting. <br/><br/>This is ‘70s Horror through and through. Expect not any major gore or jump scares. This narrative gnaws at the reader’s mind and begs the question: “What would YOU do if you suspect</span>
  <span id="freeText11201804409639248672" style="display:none">The movie adaptation of this short novel is synonymous with classic horror (and, somehow, I’ve yet to see it); the novel itself is worth a look, too. A quick, breezy ride into the occult and the destruction of a wealthy, famous family, there is a reason this story has been well-regarded for four decades and counting. <br /><br />This is ‘70s Horror through and through. Expect not any major gore or jump scares. This narrative gnaws at the reader’s mind and begs the question: “What would YOU do if you suspected your son was the anti-Christ?” There are a few strange occurrences and a couple minor gross-out moments, but on the whole this story plays in a minor key. I could have done with a bit more character development, but what is here is fine. I found myself getting a little bored at times, but on the whole I would consider this a successful horror novel. Now to see the movie. <br /><br />Read for ‘Chilling Children’ in Halloween Bingo.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3023974332" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3023974332" />
    <a title="Sud666" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666"><img alt="Sud666" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418437112p2/36890366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3023974332?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=fiction-novel">fiction-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3023974332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11711726106566853057">The Omen was a fairly popular movie. Released in 1976 it grossed over $60 million dollars and was one of the highest-grossing films of 1976. It even was nominated for two Oscars.<br/><br/>It is the archetype for many Anti-Christ stories later on. It is really a three star story, but one that gets an extra star due to its sheer impact on pop-culture.<br/><br/>The fairly unlikable Thorns are struggling to have a baby. The political climber Mr. Thorn is the US Ambassador to the UK and his manic wife, after two miscarr</span>
  <span id="freeText11711726106566853057" style="display:none">The Omen was a fairly popular movie. Released in 1976 it grossed over $60 million dollars and was one of the highest-grossing films of 1976. It even was nominated for two Oscars.<br /><br />It is the archetype for many Anti-Christ stories later on. It is really a three star story, but one that gets an extra star due to its sheer impact on pop-culture.<br /><br />The fairly unlikable Thorns are struggling to have a baby. The political climber Mr. Thorn is the US Ambassador to the UK and his manic wife, after two miscarriages have a baby. But Satan has other plans. Thorn is told his child is dead and offered a beautiful replacement, not wishing to traumatize his already manic wife, which he accepts.<br /><br />This is Damien. It has forever tainted the name "Damien" and associated it with Satan. That's not accurate since the name originates from Damianos, which is itself derived from the 4th Century Greek word damazo which meant "to tame". During this 4th century there was a St. Damien and his brother Cosmo who were martyred in Syria. He is the patron Saint of Physicians. So now you know and can name your child Damien.<br /><br />The rest of the story is a horror tory that relies more on a build-up of suspense and is more of a occult detective story. Damien is a cool kid, but doesn't say much. But, I like him due to his father and the fact he has a black German Shepherd. Very cool. <br /><br />So if you'd like to read the book about the Anti-Christ go for it. I gave it 4 stars due to cultural impact, but it truly is likely a 3 star story at best. Still, can't go wrong with a horror "classic" like this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11711726106566853057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11586148386033816584">American diplomat Jeremy Thorn adopts a strange boy named Damien when his wife Katherine delivers a stillborn child. After Damien's first nanny hangs herself, the priest that gave Damian away to Jeremy warns him that the boy will kill Katherine's unborn child. Shortly thereafter, the priest and quite a few other people surrounding Jeremy and Damian die brutal and mysterious deaths. As more and more people around Damien die in horrifying ways, Jeremy investigates Damien's background and realizes </span>
  <span id="freeText11586148386033816584" style="display:none">American diplomat Jeremy Thorn adopts a strange boy named Damien when his wife Katherine delivers a stillborn child. After Damien's first nanny hangs herself, the priest that gave Damian away to Jeremy warns him that the boy will kill Katherine's unborn child. Shortly thereafter, the priest and quite a few other people surrounding Jeremy and Damian die brutal and mysterious deaths. As more and more people around Damien die in horrifying ways, Jeremy investigates Damien's background and realizes that his adopted son may be the Antichrist.<br /><br />One of the few classic horror stories out there that actually manages to make Satan feel like a scary ass dude. I think The Omen is slightly better than The Exorcist in terms of its handling of religious horror themes, but I still think Rosemary's Baby is even better than both of them. Just like Rosemary's Baby, however, the ending of The Omen is chilling and it leaves you with the unsettling feeling that the struggles of humanity are infinitesimal in the grand scheme of greater beings. <div id="review_81510222" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81510222" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81510222?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=movie-seen">movie-seen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=part-of-series">part-of-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81510222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1594641571121739607">The Omen, by David Seltzer, was written after the film was produced. It focuses, of course, on the birth of a young boy to a successful diplomatic family who have immeasurable influence on the world. I would be surprised if you didn't know the plot already but just in case: Ambassador Robert Thorne and his wife Kathy have a child, Damien, who - at the age of 5 - begins to change. People start dying and weird warnings erupt from all sides. Robert begins suspicious and slowly begins to believe tha</span>
  <span id="freeText1594641571121739607" style="display:none">The Omen, by David Seltzer, was written after the film was produced. It focuses, of course, on the birth of a young boy to a successful diplomatic family who have immeasurable influence on the world. I would be surprised if you didn't know the plot already but just in case: Ambassador Robert Thorne and his wife Kathy have a child, Damien, who - at the age of 5 - begins to change. People start dying and weird warnings erupt from all sides. Robert begins suspicious and slowly begins to believe that his son is the antichrist.<br /><br />Plenty of suspense is cast throughout the novel; the theme is always dark and heavy on foreboding. The ending is a great climatic event, almost the entire book is used to drive up to that point.<br /><br />While nothing unbelievably shocking occurs every turn of the page, as in some novels, when something does occur it is brutal. This book is definitely not boring. I especially enjoyed the little added text from the bible that Thorn is reading, leaving us to form our own theories - while watching him form HIS.<br /><br />The little boy is shown as adorable, and yet odd. The author did an excellent job in creating the well-rounded personality the child possessed; while at times we saw him as the evil being we knew he was, our hearts cannot help but ache a bit when we read something cute and childlike he did out of confusion or innocence. The<br />mother, Kathy, is written as an overall fragile character who is overwhelmed by the current events. For a change we are not reading about the hardened, take-on-all females; she is very realistic, and also very sweet in nature. In fact, all the characters are basically likable (the ones that are on the good side of things anyway), causing a deeper sense of loss when one perishes.<br /><br />Damien isn't the main character here -- it is instead in the lap of Ambassador Thorn. He is responsible yet caring; level headed, and his feet planted firmly on earth, and yet no one can ignore the events that begin unfolding before his eyes. How he handles things is interesting and not completely predictable.<br /><br />I try and refrain from comparing films to books, but I will say that there are scenes in the novel version that were missing in the film [or added for bulk]. Mostly surrounding the photographer Jennings, who for an odd reason, is likable while his personality really isn't all that great.<br /><br />The pace is great from the start. Nothing overly climactic at the beginning but everything that happens is interesting; I never grew bored. The style isn't as simple as some other "movie-books" and for this I was glad. It all comes across well written. Nothing is overly frightening about the events, but the theme itself is deeply disturbing, and Seltzer did an excellent job transferring film to page.<br /><br />Do yourself a favor; if you enjoy religious horror or apocalyptic plots, hunt yourself down a copy of little Damien's upbringing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1594641571121739607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_223187626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223187626?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6237864-nandakishore-varma?shelf=horror">horror</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223187626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2427135762777703575">The movie of this book first introduced me to real horror - I later on became a junkie (now on withdrawal). I read the book long afterwards but was pleasantly surprised to find that even after all the suspense was taken away, the story was still disturbing and enjoyable. Kudos to Seltzer for providing hard-core Biblical horror. I never knew before that the Bible had so many poetically frightening passages. I became a fan of the Book of Revelation after reading this.<br/><br/>Damien, the lovable and angeli</span>
  <span id="freeText2427135762777703575" style="display:none">The movie of this book first introduced me to real horror - I later on became a junkie (now on withdrawal). I read the book long afterwards but was pleasantly surprised to find that even after all the suspense was taken away, the story was still disturbing and enjoyable. Kudos to Seltzer for providing hard-core Biblical horror. I never knew before that the Bible had so many poetically frightening passages. I became a fan of the Book of Revelation after reading this.<br /><br />Damien, the lovable and angelic Antichrist child is a terrific creation - so is his nurse Baylock <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(or <i>Ba' alok</i>, to use her real name) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The horror creeps, never moving into top gear, but slowly increasing in intensity. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2427135762777703575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8954352518039050812" style="display:none"> ......10 think I learned from this book.............<br /><br />1. When it appears that you have killed the monster, NEVER check to see if it's really dead.<br /><br />2. Never read a book of demon summoning aloud, even as a joke.<br /><br />3. Do not search the basement, especially if the power has gone out.<br /><br />4. If your children speak to you in Latin or any other language which they should not know, shoot them immediately. It will save you a lot of grief in the long run. However, it will probably take several rounds to kill them, so be prepared. This also applies to kids who speak with somebody else's voice.<br /><br />5. When you have the benefit of numbers, NEVER pair off or go it alone.<br /><br />6. As a general rule, don't solve puzzles that open portals to Hell.<br /><br />7. Never stand in, on, or above a grave, tomb, or crypt. This would apply to any other house of the dead as well.<br /><br />8. If you're searching for something which caused a loud noise and find out that it's just the cat, GET THE HELL OUT!<br /><br />9. If appliances start operating by themselves, do not check for short circuits just get out! <br /><br />10. Do not take ANYTHING from the dead.<br /><br /><br />thanks<br />jantu....Bossjantu<br /></span>

<div id="review_528341352" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/528341352" />
    <a title="Benjamin Stahl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl"><img alt="Benjamin Stahl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592923113p2/16968146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/528341352?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Stahl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Stahl" href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl">Benjamin Stahl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451119896" href="/book/show/1309660.The_Omen">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer528341352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11297575107769146252">Contrary to its subsequent movies, which were enjoyable enough but still fairly average, this is a relentlessly good read, and it both thrills and scares the reader consistently through its fast-paced story about a boy conceived by Satan, and his father's desperate struggle to destroy him. I liked the fact that this book didn't succumb to mainstream morality and try to make the kid a sympathetic character. I was rooting for his destruction the whole time, but I won't say how the story ends. Anyw</span>
  <span id="freeText11297575107769146252" style="display:none">Contrary to its subsequent movies, which were enjoyable enough but still fairly average, this is a relentlessly good read, and it both thrills and scares the reader consistently through its fast-paced story about a boy conceived by Satan, and his father's desperate struggle to destroy him. I liked the fact that this book didn't succumb to mainstream morality and try to make the kid a sympathetic character. I was rooting for his destruction the whole time, but I won't say how the story ends. Anyway, this was a very fun book, and its characters were much more interesting than they were in either of the movies... </span>
  <a data-text-id="11297575107769146252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13723996878515168536">I remember when the film The Omen (starring Gregory Peck) first aired on UK TV back in the early 1980s. My dad banned me from watching it because I was too young. Unperturbed, I vowed to beat this rather draconian dictum and got the book from the library. I was hooked...<br/><br/>Having watched the film many times since, I still think the book is better. The idea of an antichrist wielding so much power as a child is chilling and wonderfully horrific.   <span id="freeText13723996878515168536" style="display:none">I remember when the film The Omen (starring Gregory Peck) first aired on UK TV back in the early 1980s. My dad banned me from watching it because I was too young. Unperturbed, I vowed to beat this rather draconian dictum and got the book from the library. I was hooked...<br /><br />Having watched the film many times since, I still think the book is better. The idea of an antichrist wielding so much power as a child is chilling and wonderfully horrific. A truly psychological chiller and rather disturbing as evil prevails....I was back to the library within a week to read the Omen 2.<br /><br /><br /> </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1126467121" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15174892018894390512">This was a swift and sharp story that packed a punch, particularly for its time. I watched the original movie in anticipation for reading this and am happy to say they align closely. There were only some minor differences in details.<br/>This book only dragged for roughly one chapter where it went into a lot of depth around religious texts and doctrine. Other than this slump, the book had good pacing and jumped right into the drama.<br/>If you are an old school horror fan - pick this one up!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1813588509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1813588509" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1813588509?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=horror-2016">horror-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1813588509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8916194941612076957">I read this for November's Horror Aficionados read. <br/><br/><b>Please note that I gave this book 3.5 stars and rounded it up to 4 stars on Goodreads.</b><br/><br/>This was a good horror book, but my mind tended to wander the entire story-line. I think the problem is that the writing style was just okay, and a few times there would be a sentence or two that just read wrong in my head and I would get distracted.<br/><br/>This book is kind of a weird thing in itself. This was released two weeks prior to the movie being released. The</span>
  <span id="freeText8916194941612076957" style="display:none">I read this for November's Horror Aficionados read. <br /><br /><b>Please note that I gave this book 3.5 stars and rounded it up to 4 stars on Goodreads.</b><br /><br />This was a good horror book, but my mind tended to wander the entire story-line. I think the problem is that the writing style was just okay, and a few times there would be a sentence or two that just read wrong in my head and I would get distracted.<br /><br />This book is kind of a weird thing in itself. This was released two weeks prior to the movie being released. There were some minor changes between the book/movie, but ultimately this whole book read like a very jazzed up screenplay. I don't want to make comparisons between Dan Brown or David Seltzer, but a few times I would read something and could see the scene in my head from the movie. So Seltzer definitely wins when it comes to tying the book/movie together.<br /><br />The Omen follows Robert Thorn and his wife Katherine after the birth of their son. Readers are quickly hip to the fact that Katherine and Robert's child is murdered by mysterious persons and is switched with another baby. Robert is led to believe that his baby was stillborn and is talked into switching out his baby with another baby whose mother died. The set-up to why Robert would do such a thing is that the book goes more into Katherine's mental state prior to this birth and how fragile she was due to the miscarriages she had prior to giving birth.<br /><br />So this whole book is really just Katherine and Robert realizing that their son Damien does not seem to be like other boys and Robert realizing that something dark seems to be stalking his family.<br /><br />The writing as I said was good but certain parts were a bit much here and there. This book included pictures from the 2006 film staring Julia Stiles and Liev Schrieber. It was actually odd that the book threw some photos in there randomly in the book. It broke up the flow of my reading. I wish that they had inserted the pictures at the end of the book, or if you are going to insert the pictures in the book, insert them in where the picture references what is going on in the story at that time. Since the book itself that I have is pretty old looking, it was weird to see the glossy colored pictures as well.<br /><br />There are other books in this series, but I am going to pass on them. All in all some of the imagery in the book was gruesome here and there so that's fair warning to those out there looking for something like this to read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8916194941612076957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rade " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8187431-rade"><img alt="Rade " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426096920p2/8187431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/953028138?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rade " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rade " href="/user/show/8187431-rade">Rade </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8187431-rade?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer953028138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2400923611637730835">A story about a father who instead of being the happiest he can be, is instead put through hell (ha!) when his son turns out to be a lot darker than he appears. A lot of signs are there that he is not a normal kid, but his parents chalk it down to him being a young child who is still adjusting to a new family. As the story progresses, his father becomes obsessed with getting to the bottom of the mystery of his son, while around him a lot of people get into "accidents."<br/><br/>Overall a very enjoyable re</span>
  <span id="freeText2400923611637730835" style="display:none">A story about a father who instead of being the happiest he can be, is instead put through hell (ha!) when his son turns out to be a lot darker than he appears. A lot of signs are there that he is not a normal kid, but his parents chalk it down to him being a young child who is still adjusting to a new family. As the story progresses, his father becomes obsessed with getting to the bottom of the mystery of his son, while around him a lot of people get into "accidents."<br /><br />Overall a very enjoyable read and as a plus there were about 6 pages of stills from the 1976 movie in the middle of the book. I got to admit that if someone looks at those stills before reading the book, it will totally ruin the story as it depicts some of the key moments from the book. The 1976 movie was very faithful to the actual story so after reading the book, go see the movie. A bit old for the younger crowd who prefer modern movies, but a great classic nonetheless. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2400923611637730835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ay0/+RVBd85NktWPMNgHfwRgd2XqQVHfD8y+cAIPHd92ZqP2uVf2T2z1re2sFQv4rMc6i0nySC83p92b329g4w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VqsNC9xLS7llByzr/W535bEOZ/ox6M5/rJ3MW4V4Vd0j4JEEcF3KOERgVIlho3tiGakqFJJb14+U9q+wWBgo4Q==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer16097555895271122752">David Seltzer (born 1940) is an American screenwriter, novelist, producer and director, perhaps best known for writing <i>The Omen</i> (1976), and <i>Bird on a Wire</i> (1990). As writer-director, Seltzer's credits include the 1986 teen tragi-comedy <i>Lucas</i> starring Corey Haim, Charlie Sheen and Winona Ryder, the 1988 comedy <i>Punchline</i> starring Sally Field and Tom Hanks, and 1992's <i> Shining Through</i> starring Melani</span>
  <span id="freeText16097555895271122752" style="display:none">David Seltzer (born 1940) is an American screenwriter, novelist, producer and director, perhaps best known for writing <i>The Omen</i> (1976), and <i>Bird on a Wire</i> (1990). As writer-director, Seltzer's credits include the 1986 teen tragi-comedy <i>Lucas</i> starring Corey Haim, Charlie Sheen and Winona Ryder, the 1988 comedy <i>Punchline</i> starring Sally Field and Tom Hanks, and 1992's <i> Shining Through</i> starring Melanie Griffith and Michael Douglas.</span>
